The question seeks to clarify which molecular targets are amenable to detection by this assay format.", 'hypothetical_answer': 'Indicator Displacement Assays (IDAs) are versatile analytical techniques used to detect a wide variety of molecules. In an IDA, a receptor is pre-bound to a colorimetric or fluorescent indicator. When a target analyte (the molecule of interest) is introduced, it competes with the indicator for binding to the receptor, displacing the indicator and causing a measurable change in color or fluorescence. The types of molecules that can be detected by IDA include: \n\n- Metal ions (e.g., Zn²⁺, Cu²⁺, Fe³⁺, Pb²⁺, Hg²⁺)\n- Small organic molecules (e.g., amino acids, sugars, neurotransmitters, drugs)\n- Anions (e.g., phosphate, sulfate, nitrate, fluoride, chloride)\n- Peptides and small proteins (when appropriate receptors are used)\n- Nucleotides and nucleic acids (in specialized IDA formats)\n\nThe versatility of IDA arises from the ability to design or select receptors with high specificity for the target analyte. The choice of indicator and receptor determines the selectivity and sensitivity of the assay. IDAs are widely used in environmental monitoring, clinical diagnostics, and biochemical research for the detection and quantification of diverse molecular species.', 'key_concepts': In an IDA, a receptor is pre-bound to a colorimetric or fluorescent indicator. When a target analyte (the molecule of interest) is introduced, it competes with the indicator for binding to the receptor, displacing the indicator and causing a measurable change in color or fluorescence. The types of molecules that can be detected by IDA include: \n\n- Metal ions (e.g., Zn²⁺, Cu²⁺, Fe³⁺, Pb²⁺, Hg²⁺)\n- Small organic molecules (e.g., amino acids, sugars, neurotransmitters, drugs)\n- Anions (e.g., phosphate, sulfate, nitrate, fluoride, chloride)\n- Peptides and small proteins (when appropriate receptors are used)\n- Nucleotides and nucleic acids (in specialized IDA formats)\n\nThe versatility of IDA arises from the ability to design or select receptors with high specificity for the target analyte. The choice of indicator and receptor determines the selectivity and sensitivity of the assay. In an IDA, a receptor is pre-bound to a colorimetric or fluorescent indicator. When a target analyte (the molecule of interest) is introduced, it competes with the indicator for binding to the receptor, displacing the indicator and causing a measurable change in color or fluorescence. The types of molecules that can be detected by IDA include: \n\n- Metal ions (e.g., Zn²⁺, Cu²⁺, Fe³⁺, Pb²⁺, Hg²⁺)\n- Small organic molecules (e.g., amino acids, sugars, neurotransmitters, drugs)\n- Anions (e.g., phosphate, sulfate, nitrate, fluoride, chloride)\n- Peptides and small proteins (when appropriate receptors are used)\n- Nucleotides and nucleic acids (in specialized IDA formats)\n\nThe versatility of IDA arises from the ability to design or select receptors with high specificity for the target analyte. The choice of indicator and receptor determines the selectivity and sensitivity of the assay. IDAs are widely used in environmental monitoring, clinical diagnostics, and biochemical research for the detection and quantification of diverse molecular species.', 'key_concepts': In an IDA, a receptor is pre-bound to a colorimetric or fluorescent indicator. When a target analyte (the molecule of interest) is introduced, it competes with the indicator for binding to the receptor, displacing the indicator and causing a measurable change in color or fluorescence. The types of molecules that can be detected by IDA include: \n\n- Metal ions (e.g., Zn²⁺, Cu²⁺, Fe³⁺, Pb²⁺, Hg²⁺)\n- Small organic molecules (e.g., amino acids, sugars, neurotransmitters, drugs)\n- Anions (e.g., phosphate, sulfate, nitrate, fluoride, chloride)\n- Peptides and small proteins (when appropriate receptors are used)\n- Nucleotides and nucleic acids (in specialized IDA formats)\n\nThe versatility of IDA arises from the ability to design or select receptors with high specificity for the target analyte. The choice of indicator and receptor determines the selectivity and sensitivity of the assay. IDAs are widely used in environmental monitoring, clinical diagnostics, and biochemical research for the detection and quantification of diverse molecular species.', 'key_concepts':
